It's the End of the Year As We Know It
======================================



 Posted in [Command Tower](/en/articles/columns/command-tower-archive)
 on December 11, 2014 






![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/styles/auth_small/public/images/person/authorpic_adamstyborski.jpg)
By Adam Styborski




 Stybs has played Magic the world over, writing and drafting as part of the event coverage team and slinging Commander everywhere his decks will fit. 





This was a big year for our favorite format: 10 multicolor Gods; 5 Planeswalkers; 23 more new legendary creatures. In just one year we were faced with 38 new choices for building a new deck. It was a bigger gift than I could have ever expected.


![](https://media.wizards.com/2014/images/daily/cardart_infernalspawnofinfernalspawnofevil.jpg)

[Infernal Spawn of Infernal Spawn of Evil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Spawn+of+Infernal+Spawn+of+Evil) | Art by [Ron Spencer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?action=advanced&artist=["Ron+Spencer"])



If you're expecting more than 30 decks to appear below you vastly overestimate how many decks can reasonably fit into one Commander article. What it does set up, however, is an opportunity to reflect on what you've done in your format over the past twelve months.



Building my Religion
====================



While I've personally gone through about a dozen different decks and commanders over the past year, I've also shared them with you along the way. [Mogis, God of Slaughter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogis%2C+God+of+Slaughter); [Pharika, God of Affliction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pharika%2C+God+of+Affliction); and [Prossh, Skyraider of Kher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prossh%2C+Skyraider+of+Kher) have all inspired and influenced my builds at fundamental levels and led me to sharing some of the best ideas that's come from playing with such a great community.



Now it's time to unleash some of your best decks and the reasons they've made a difference for you, starting with Andrew:



This year was rough for me when it comes to Commander. So many new decks, so many sleeves purchases. I've put together decks for [Kurkesh, Onakke Ancient](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kurkesh%2C+Onakke+Ancient); [Glissa, the Traitor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glissa%2C+the+Traitor); [Sliver Queen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sliver+Queen); [Nahiri, the Lithomancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nahiri%2C+the+Lithomancer); and retooled all my old decks. My favorite new deck, however, belongs to [Surrak Dragonclaw](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surrak+Dragonclaw).



[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Surrak+Dragonclaw)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Surrak+Dragonclaw)



Don't let the Sultai lie to you or the Jeskai trick you: Temur clan is best clan. I love creatures, so it was clear to me that a Temur deck was going to be built. I started by listing every blue, red, and green creature I would include in the deck. Two hundred cards later, it was time to start editing.



I broke my list into five categories: Beatsticks, Critter Removal, Noncritter Removal, Mana Dorks, and Support. Then I had a second list simply called Spells for the whopping nine noncreature, nonland cards this deck was going to include.



It's been an absolute blast to play. There is no subtlety here; I'm going to beat your face in with big fat fatties or die trying. It's a deck that drips with power, putting some of the most frightening creature cards in Commander together into one deck. It runs out of the gate and never slows down. Ultimately, this has been one of the most fun deck-building challenges and most fun decks to play in my Commander tenure. Here's the list:

99 Cards 



![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Surrak+Dragonclaw)



















Chris here, and my favorite new deck is a [Zurgo Helmsmasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zurgo+Helmsmasher) deck I put together when I got bored of my [Prossh, Skyraider of Kher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prossh%2C+Skyraider+of+Kher) deck. It's a powerful, aggressive deck built more around card quality than combos, and is difficult for my opponents to interact with.



[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Zurgo+Helmsmasher)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zurgo+Helmsmasher)



Plan A is to cast [Zurgo Helmsmasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zurgo+Helmsmasher), suit him up with Equipment, and bash. He is a powerful threat that can win games quickly through commander damage, so my opponents have to deal with him. More importantly, he distracts my opponents from the real threat—all the other creatures in the deck. All the Equipment work well with him, but [Assault Suit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assault+Suit) is particularly great with an indestructible commander who must attack.



Besides a few utility creatures ([Burnished Hart](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burnished+Hart), [Heliod's Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heliod%27s+Pilgrim), [Necrotic Sliver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Necrotic+Sliver), [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum)) every creature is a powerful threat that can win the game by itself, and all carry Equipment well. Add in a reanimation/graveyard-recursion suite and a pile of spell lands, and this "aggressive" deck can play a long grindy game with the best of them.



Since this deck is all about combat, it runs more removal than I typically see in other people's decks. I also run a large number of tutors, which lets me fetch a wide range of silver bullets for difficulty board states ([Arcane Lighthouse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arcane+Lighthouse), [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment), [Steel Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Hellkite), [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), etc.). And of course, assembling [Cabal Coffers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Coffers) + [Urborg, Tomb of Yawgmoth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urborg%2C+Tomb+of+Yawgmoth) is always fun.



Finally, this is the best [Opal Palace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Opal+Palace) deck I've ever played. Not only does it make Zurgo much more threatening in the late game, but the deck runs lots of other colorless spell lands and really values the fixing.








#### Chris's Zurgo


#####

99 Cards 



![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Zurgo+Helmsmasher)




















This one utilized [Narset, Enlightened Master](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narset%2C+Enlightened+Master) to wreak havoc, with no other creature cards in it. Rather, it has many ways of boosting Narset into an unstoppable Monk, with power unmatched by Dragons.



[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Narset%2C+Enlightened+Master)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narset%2C+Enlightened+Master)



The deck uses mana artifacts to get the commander on board early, while most of these artifacts also provide additional utility: some can be sacrificed for extra cards ([Cluestones](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?output=spoiler&method=visual&name=+[Cluestone]), [Commander's Sphere](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Commander%27s+Sphere), [Dreamstone Hedron](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreamstone+Hedron)), some can turn into creatures (Azorius Keyrune), most are useful when someone can force you to sacrifice Narset. The deck also boasts of a solid enchantment-based defense ([Ghostly Prison](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghostly+Prison), [Propaganda](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Propaganda), [Teferi's Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Teferi%27s+Moat)) to discourage early aggression against you. Once enough mana is built up, one of the mass destructions can be used to wipe out all lands—the deck also boasts of a good selection of mass removals. If you'd lack artifacts, Narset can still cast spells for free—anything that is not a land in the deck is a free card for your use at every attack.



Narset's protection is guaranteed by enchantments like [Gift of Immortality](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gift+of+Immortality), [Flickerform](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flickerform), or enchantments with [totem armor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?output=spoiler&method=visual&text=+[%22totem+armor%22]), while her base hexproof saves us the card slots for Commander staples such as [Swiftfoot Boots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swiftfoot+Boots) and [Lightning Greaves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Greaves). Various spells also have scry, making sure that Narset's swings use up as many cards as possible. There are also a few late-game options that could turn the tide easily—once [Flickerform](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flickerform) is on board (also tutorable with [Three Dreams](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Three+Dreams)), an [Evacuation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evacuation), or a [Decree of Annihilation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Decree+of+Annihilation) can leave the board in a state where victory is inevitable even without the deck's [Insurrection](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Insurrection). And trust me, with this deck—it really is.








#### Martin's Narset


#####

99 Cards 



![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Narset%2C+Enlightened+Master)




















I've enjoyed my War of the Gods deck the most. It's not the strongest of decks, clearly, as the mana base is extremely finicky and fragile (a single [Ruination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination) and I'm pretty much wiped) and isn't an early-aggro deck, but it does have a lot of fun and does a number of cool things. I built it around all of the Gods, and then included most of the Avatars and Lieges from *Shadowmoor*/*Eventide* to ensure getting the [Gods](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?output=spoiler&method=visual&action=advanced&format=+[%22Theros+Block%22]&subtype=+[God]) active as soon as possible (as well as some key *Ravnica*-block cards which are also hybrid mana—Privileged Position, what a champ). I'm still tinkering with it (always tinkering) but it's been a blast to play. Originally, it had Karona (the False God!) as the commander, but I found I was never ever casting her, and [Child of Alara](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Alara) is an Avatar (still on theme) and it's nice to have a last resort, blow up the world on tap.








#### Cliff's War of the Gods


#####

99 Cards 



![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=CHILD+OF+ALARA)




















My favorite commander deck I made this year is my new Abzan commander.



[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Anafenza%2C+the+Foremost)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Anafenza%2C+the+Foremost)



There're a few reasons why:



1. First, it boosts the power of creatures to scary sizes with +1/+1 counters.
2. Second, it creates an army of tokens through various cards that also work with +1/+1 counters, like [Mycoloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mycoloth).
3. Third, it also provides great protection behind powerful control cards.
4. The board wipes aren't plentiful, but will pack a big punch when you draw them.
5. The biggest reason: the massive amount of lifegain!









#### Taner's Anafenza


##### 




[![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)](/en/decklist/deck-list-d561c4ad871c18541ce81844317f5128.txt?n=Taner%27s%20Anafenza)





[Decklist](#none)
[Stats](#none)
[Sample Hand](#none)

COMMANDER:
 Anafenza, the Foremost

1

99 Cards 



![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Anafenza%2C+the+Foremost)



















This is my [Sidisi, Brood Tyrant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sidisi%2C+Brood+Tyrant) Commander deck. It is the first Commander deck I've ever built, and I did it by a wish to make a deck that was not as competitive, but durdly and fun. I've gotten 40 Zombies at one point, and have almost milled myself with a giant [Decree of Pain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Decree+of+Pain), then [Oversold Cemetery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oversold+Cemetery)-ed back [Loaming Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Loaming+Shaman) to keep myself alive.



[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sidisi%2C+Brood+Tyrant)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sidisi%2C+Brood+Tyrant)



I've only played about ten games, give or take, with it, but at least four of them were more fun than any Standard game I've played in a while. I'm already thinking about making a five-color defender deck (with maybe [Cromat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cromat) as commander, if there aren't any other cool five-color commanders) with [Flamewright](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flamewright), [Vent Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vent+Sentinel), [Axebane Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Axebane+Guardian), and other stuff.



Commander is the best format I've been introduced to this year. Commander is eternal, and nearly everybody at my shop plays it. All the games are fun, and I'll never get old of it.



So, I'd love to give a shout out to Braidan & the other guys at [Crazy Timmy's](http://www.crazytimmy.com) to introduce me to this possibility, and a great format.







#### Alex's Sidisi


##### 




[![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)](/en/decklist/deck-list-6249d5d2babded61d3fb96c18bb0a7d8.txt?n=Alex%27s%20Sidisi)

99 Cards 



![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sidisi%2C+Brood+Tyrant)




















When *Innistrad* came out a few years ago, I wanted to build Commander decks around [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) and Grimgrin. Sadly, I couldn't get either to work out to my satisfaction so I shelved them. A few months back, *Conspiracy* was released. I saw [Marchesa, the Black Rose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marchesa%2C+the+Black+Rose) and knew she was just perfect for me. Olivia and Grimgrin? Oh why keep them apart when they can now be partners in crime. Basically, the deck is never-ending value because Marchesa brings them back.



[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Marchesa%2C+the+Black+Rose)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marchesa%2C+the+Black+Rose)



[Mikaeus, the Unhallowed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mikaeus%2C+the+Unhallowed) and [Flayer of the Hatebound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flayer+of+the+Hatebound) often compete for the best creature in the deck. Undying in general makes Marchesa very happy. [Triskelion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Triskelion) combos off with [Mephidross Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mephidross+Vampire) for a board wipe or with Mikaeus to wipe the table. Sacrifice outlets like Lyzolda, Grimgrin, and flashing back [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return) break Marchesa wide open. Several creatures act as removal spells themselves. Combat is difficult for opponents because of Marchesa's ability.



I have two tutor effects mostly for recovering Marchesa from tuck effects like [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus) and [Oblation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblation). [Unspeakable Symbol](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unspeakable+Symbol) and [Feast on the Fallen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Feast+on+the+Fallen) are all-stars in the deck and are essentially free ways to get +1/+1 counters on my creatures. [Grave Betrayal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grave+Betrayal) is borderline unfair in conjunction with Marchesa.



It's all value, all the time. I know it's vulnerable to graveyard hate like [Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace) or [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void) but I can live with that. That just means I have to kill them first. Either way, I have tons of fun running with the boss, Marchesa.



I'd honestly like to add a 37th land, [Stalking Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stalking+Vengeance), and [Living Death](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Living+Death) (a card I actually forgot about when building Marchesa).








#### Emmett's Marchesa

99 Cards 



![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Marchesa%2C+the+Black+Rose)




















The deck I built this year that captured my heart the most has got to be my [Selvala, Explorer Returned](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selvala%2C+Explorer+Returned) deck.



[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Selvala%2C+Explorer+Returned)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selvala%2C+Explorer+Returned)



Way back when *Conspiracy* came out you asked us about new legendary creatures we wanted to build around, and at the time I only had a vague idea of what was going to go into my Selvala fog deck. Several bad cards went in, most of them were taken out for other bad cards, which were in turn taken out for bad cards that made me smile. But through it all the core of the deck remained the same: draw cards, gain life, figure it out from there.



The deck has eleven [Fog](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fog)-type cards, not counting flashback and instant-speed mass removal. It has enough targeted removal to deal with non-attacking threats. And it has things like Ulamog and [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus) when the game needs to end. But the best part about the deck is the number of (at least for my group) silly cards it's running. [Purity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Purity) was included because it had "prevent damage" on it, but then it became the coolest thing ever against the two Purphoros decks in my group. [Tempt with Discovery](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempt+with+Discovery) and [Act of Authority](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Act+of+Authority) are cards that involve my opponents and never fail to cause them to grumble. The lands are hilarious; yes, [Kabira Crossroads](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kabira+Crossroads) and [Radiant Fountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Radiant+Fountain) are Commander playable. And I do not even remember how many games [Felidar Sovereign](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Felidar+Sovereign) has won me (I wanna say five).



It's control without blue, it's the most unassuming thing at the table, and it has made me happier than I ever thought a random deck idea could.







#### Bobby's Selvala


##### 




[![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)](/en/decklist/deck-list-b5ae35709803acca6d4941b4a866195b.txt?n=Bobby%27s%20Selvala)

That's it. Pure, unfiltered Commander awesome from across the community. It's a been a great year for the format, and I'm excited to say that there's even more awesome on the horizon when *Fate Reforged* previews begin in a couple weeks.



The next two weeks feature reruns of some of the biggest articles of the year, and I'll be back to start a brand-new year in the most literal fashion. Wherever you are and whatever you choose to celebrate, I hope you're as excited as I am for what's in store down the road.



Commander is, always, what you choose to make of it. Thanks for letting me make it all about you. See you in 2015!
